  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_f2e5facd-2af8-4e64-a2c8-0e1138a8d62b'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();

      initializeSiwa();

<span class='communityAnswererName'>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">So far the answers on here have stated that the tv series were not that different. I beg to differ. I have watched the whole series & read the book. B<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">So far the answers on here have stated that the tv series were not that different. I beg to differ. I have watched the whole series &amp; read the book. Basically the only thing the same are some of the characters names &amp; somewhat the ending. They used the name of the book &amp; the basic ( very loosely) ending. The book will be very different &amp; at times a little slow, but well worth the read. The show is nice, but basically is not the story in the book.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

<div id="review_33509781" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/33509781" />
    <a title="Lucy " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45923-lucy"><img alt="Lucy " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1300985055p2/45923.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/33509781?book_show_action=true">Sep 22, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lucy " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lucy " href="/user/show/45923-lucy">Lucy </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/4712753-the-elfstones-of-shannara">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45923-lucy?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45923-lucy?shelf=childhood-favorites">childhood-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45923-lucy?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45923-lucy?shelf=epic-fantasy">epic-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer33509781" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17985920494727160417">I don't think you can possibly understand what a formative impact this book had on me.<br/><br/>Picture it: I was nine years old. We were at this massive used book sale, and I was bored silly of all the books at the children's table. I wandered around a bit, and ended up in adult SF/F. And there, like a shining beacon of fascinating glory, was a gorgeous hardcover copy of The Elfstones of Shannara.<br/><br/>Of course I bought it, even though my parents thought I wouldn't understand it. And they were right. I didn't</span>
  <span id="freeText17985920494727160417" style="display:none">I don't think you can possibly understand what a formative impact this book had on me.<br /><br />Picture it: I was nine years old. We were at this massive used book sale, and I was bored silly of all the books at the children's table. I wandered around a bit, and ended up in adult SF/F. And there, like a shining beacon of fascinating glory, was a gorgeous hardcover copy of The Elfstones of Shannara.<br /><br />Of course I bought it, even though my parents thought I wouldn't understand it. And they were right. I didn't understand it. I didn't pick up on half of the subtext, the subtleties.<br /><br />But I loved it. I loved the sweeping adventure and the epic feel and the heroic yet human characters. I loved the magic and the loss and the battles and the struggles. I loved every single page of it.<br /><br />And that's how I became a fantasy addict.<br /><br />I know this book isn't perfect. I've heard people say it's derivative, and it probably is. But for me, this book, this series (because of course, as soon as I discovered that there were more, I read all of them--Sword of Shannara, Wishsong of Shannara, and my favorite, the Heritage of Shannara quartet--which, by the way, was how I discovered that there was a whole SECTION of fantasy books in the bookstore--so much more to read, so many more adventures to explore!) captivated my imagination and lured me into fantasy.<br /><br />In my mind, this book is perfect. And for me, yes, it does stand the test of time. Every time I reread it--every few years--I find that while I am rereading the story, I am also reliving that magical experience as a nine-year-old of discovering magic and adventure and wonder. I now own a paperback edition for easy carrying around, but I still have that beautiful old hardcover, with its maps and line-drawings and solid presence in my lap.<br /><br />For me, this book will always be perfect.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17985920494727160417" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1489470593" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7355023176229232225">[1 Star] Starting off 2016 with a bang. I hope that's not indicative of how this year will go for me. <br/><br/>This book is definitely not for me. At first, I was intrigued. The world was cool enough. The story, promising. But soon I started to like the book less and less as I read it. The writing was not for me. It is insanely repetitive. The same story is told over and over and over. The same story is told over and over and over. The foreshadowing is clunky and blatant. Watch out! This character has so</span>
  <span id="freeText7355023176229232225" style="display:none">[1 Star] Starting off 2016 with a bang. I hope that's not indicative of how this year will go for me. <br /><br />This book is definitely not for me. At first, I was intrigued. The world was cool enough. The story, promising. But soon I started to like the book less and less as I read it. The writing was not for me. It is insanely repetitive. The same story is told over and over and over. The same story is told over and over and over. The foreshadowing is clunky and blatant. Watch out! This character has something mysterious that he will reveal in two chapters. You would only have to read the dialogue and one sentence per paragraph to know exactly what was happening which if we're being honest, isn't that much. It is predictable and so cheesy. The characters are very flat to me. I did not care about a single one of them. Overall, not a very enjoyable book, and I started skimming toward the end to just be done. <br /><br />I don't recommend this book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7355023176229232225" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3520795770868272021">Every bit as fascinating, fantastical and phenomenal as the first book!<br/><br/>I was initially disappointed that this did not feature the same characters from the first installment in the trilogy, and that we would not get to see how their lives had continued to develop after the close of the book. So much time had passed between the two, in fact, that this felt more like a companion novel than a continuation of the series.<br/><br/>I soon forgot the prior adventure had even existed, however, as I was sucked into</span>
  <span id="freeText3520795770868272021" style="display:none">Every bit as fascinating, fantastical and phenomenal as the first book!<br /><br />I was initially disappointed that this did not feature the same characters from the first installment in the trilogy, and that we would not get to see how their lives had continued to develop after the close of the book. So much time had passed between the two, in fact, that this felt more like a companion novel than a continuation of the series.<br /><br />I soon forgot the prior adventure had even existed, however, as I was sucked into this new surreal and incredible journey. This current set of characters became just as beloved, the world just as awe-inspiring and the adventures just as hair-raising and incredulous.<br /><br />Brooks has well-and-truly proven himself a new favourite of mine!</span>

<div id="review_278717265" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/278717265" />
    <a title="Stefan Yates" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7590340-stefan-yates"><img alt="Stefan Yates" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1328116275p2/7590340.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/278717265?book_show_action=true">Feb 16, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stefan Yates" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stefan Yates" href="/user/show/7590340-stefan-yates">Stefan Yates</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780345302533" href="/book/show/3731932-the-elfstones-of-shannara">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7590340-stefan-yates?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7590340-stefan-yates?shelf=stefan-dusty-bookshelf-2014">stefan-dusty-bookshelf-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7590340-stefan-yates?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer278717265" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer396673429934002725">As with the Sword of Shannara, I must preface this review by stating that I do not know why there is so much loathing of this series. I find these books to be well-written, nicely paced, epic fantasy that work well together or even as stand-alone entries. <br/><br/>One of the coolest things to me about this series is that you always get a new set of main characters. The stories relate to one another, but they are separated by many years and a new generation has to step up to face the current threat. While</span>
  <span id="freeText396673429934002725" style="display:none">As with the Sword of Shannara, I must preface this review by stating that I do not know why there is so much loathing of this series. I find these books to be well-written, nicely paced, epic fantasy that work well together or even as stand-alone entries. <br /><br />One of the coolest things to me about this series is that you always get a new set of main characters. The stories relate to one another, but they are separated by many years and a new generation has to step up to face the current threat. While I do enjoy tales that follow the same main character or characters, I find this to be a refreshing departure from normal fare. I enjoy Mr. Brooks' writing quite a bit and find his world building to be top notch. <br /><br />If you haven't given the Shannara Series a chance because of all of the negative vibe concerning its similarities to The Lord of the Rings, you really owe it to yourself to give it a shot. You may end up not liking it and that is fine, but I find the series to be very enjoyable and have plenty of its own unique merit to be able to stand on its own.</span>
  <a data-text-id="396673429934002725" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Angie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2687901-angie"><img alt="Angie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1459874153p2/2687901.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/128893308?book_show_action=true">Nov 01, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angie" href="/user/show/2687901-angie">Angie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781857231106" href="/book/show/15565.The_Elfstones_of_Shannara">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fantasy lovers</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2687901-angie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer128893308" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14902871447820910920">I loved this book. I was a bit disappointed at the beginning when I realized that I wouldn't be reading about Shea, Flick, and Balinor, but I quickly became used to Wil and Amberle, and frankly, I found them to be much more believable and relatable characters. Shea and Flick were a bit annoying at times, and the other characters were too close to LoTR characters for me to really get close to them. This book could stand on its own, and it was a good story.<br/><br/>I enjoyed the character development of An</span>
  <span id="freeText14902871447820910920" style="display:none">I loved this book. I was a bit disappointed at the beginning when I realized that I wouldn't be reading about Shea, Flick, and Balinor, but I quickly became used to Wil and Amberle, and frankly, I found them to be much more believable and relatable characters. Shea and Flick were a bit annoying at times, and the other characters were too close to LoTR characters for me to really get close to them. This book could stand on its own, and it was a good story.<br /><br />I enjoyed the character development of Ander. I think he is a wonderful replacement for Eventine. I think most people can relate to him because most of us are just normal people who rise to the occasion when responsibility is thrust upon us. Ander carried that burden well, and I think he will be as beloved as his father before him.<br /><br />However, I do have a couple of complaints about Brooks' writing style: he's a bit repetitive and a bit too descriptive at times. I have read about hundreds of battles and been introduced to so many new fantasy worlds—but I think Brooks was one of the most descriptive writers, which is saying a lot. However, the writing in this book was better than the writing in the first book, though I did find a couple of grammatical errors.<br /><br />The ending was very satisfying. For me, an ending isn't great unless it comes with that bittersweet feeling. The love story between Wil and Amberle enjoyable, and it was just heart-wrenching to see it end the way it did. I wanted them to hook up, partly so that the Ohmsfords could start adding a bit more Elven blood to the Shannara line. However, it is good that Eretria went home with Wil. She was a good match for Wil, even if I was rooting for Amberle the entire time. All in all, a very satisfying ending.<br /><br />I hope the next end-of-the-world crisis doesn't happen too far into the future; I'm not ready to say goodbye to these characters yet.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14902871447820910920" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

<span id="freeTextContainer423538245409096871">Brooks was finding his own voice with this one, probably because there wasn't much left to crib from Tolkien after he wrote <i>The Sword of Shannara</i> (although we still get a Shadowfax-type horse, giant flying birds, and tree people). <br/><br/>I felt that this volume was much slower than the last one, with long stretches of not much happening. When something does happen, however, Brooks really knows how to write a gripping scene. <br/><br/>For as many complaints that I have with Terry Brooks, I can't deny that his boo</span>
  <span id="freeText423538245409096871" style="display:none">Brooks was finding his own voice with this one, probably because there wasn't much left to crib from Tolkien after he wrote <i>The Sword of Shannara</i> (although we still get a Shadowfax-type horse, giant flying birds, and tree people). <br /><br />I felt that this volume was much slower than the last one, with long stretches of not much happening. When something does happen, however, Brooks really knows how to write a gripping scene. <br /><br />For as many complaints that I have with Terry Brooks, I can't deny that his books make me feel like a kid discovering epic fantasy for the first time. This is true old school fantasy, which is rarely done well anymore. <br /></span>

<div id="review_1589707626" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1589707626" />
    <a title="Wendy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4598314-wendy"><img alt="Wendy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1391090778p2/4598314.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1589707626?book_show_action=true">Mar 24, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wendy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wendy" href="/user/show/4598314-wendy">Wendy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780808522652" href="/book/show/2115773.The_Elfstones_of_Shannara">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4598314-wendy?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4598314-wendy?shelf=movies-and-tv">movies-and-tv</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4598314-wendy?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1589707626" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13552610762457189759">I read this specifically because I wanted to compare it to the television series, which I recently watched. Otherwise, I really had no intention of returning to Shannara. I read LOTR 2.0 -- I mean, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15575.The_Sword_of_Shannara__The_Original_Shannara_Trilogy___1_' title='The Sword of Shannara (The Original Shannara Trilogy, #1) by Terry Brooks' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Sword of Shannara</a>, and was bored. Were it not for the fact that I was actually watching paint dry at the time (repainting my kitchen) and being entertained by my co-blogger, Tiara, who had recently undertaken the same journey, I am not sure how I would have survived the trip. But what actually tur</span>
  <span id="freeText13552610762457189759" style="display:none">I read this specifically because I wanted to compare it to the television series, which I recently watched. Otherwise, I really had no intention of returning to Shannara. I read LOTR 2.0 -- I mean, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15575.The_Sword_of_Shannara__The_Original_Shannara_Trilogy___1_" title="The Sword of Shannara (The Original Shannara Trilogy, #1) by Terry Brooks" rel="nofollow noopener">The Sword of Shannara</a>, and was bored. Were it not for the fact that I was actually watching paint dry at the time (repainting my kitchen) and being entertained by my co-blogger, Tiara, who had recently undertaken the same journey, I am not sure how I would have survived the trip. But what actually turned out to be a respectable show, despite being housed on MTV, was enough to inspire me to revisit this post-apocalyptic world to, well, see what new apocalypse was on the way.<br /><br />This time, Shay Ohmsford's grandson is doing Allanon's manipulative bidding to save the world from evil. The Ellcrys, the great tree that holds back the demon hordes, is dying. To save it, its seed must be replanted by a chosen one. But conveniently, the demons have slaughtered the chosen ones--save for the young elven princess, Amberle, with whose care Allanon charges Wil Ohmsford, the current bearer of the elfstones. Can Wil and Amberle make it to Safehold and figure out what to do with the seed and the bloodfire? Will the elf army be able to hold off the demon horde until they do? <br /><br />I'm not going to lie. Watching the show greatly enhanced what is otherwise an interesting, but still pretty dull journey. It's like playing an RPG video game and slogging through all those grind-y moments with characters I just didn't care about. Amberle and Wil are just plain dull, no matter how much life and emotion Brooks tries to infuse into them and their growing relationship with each other. Thankfully, the Rover girl Eretria adds some much needed fire to the threesome, which the show plays up for good reason. Wil and Amberle alone fizzle, but with Eretria in their midst, there's a bit more potential which the show takes advantage of by aging up the characters and letting them have of the sex, and, more importantly, allows them to form a strong bond of friendship between the three of them.<br /><br />It also helps that the show gives me lovely visuals of Allanon to work with, in the form of Manu Bennett. I was pleasantly surprised to meet the eleven prince, Ander Elessedil as well. Many characters get more face time in the Chronicles of Shannara in order to express themselves (including the bad guy, the Dagda Mor, who is little more than a named end boss in the book). I didn't expect, when watching the show, that Ander would play such a prominent role in terms of screen time, but I am glad this focus on his character remained true to its source as Ander struggles with his potential as heir to the throne, and leader of the elven army against the demons threatening to destroy everything. <br /><br />Did Brooks' writing improve in the second book? His prose is a bit tighter, but his plotting still relies on letting his main characters plod along, with their journey frequently interrupted by the monster of the week. This is, of course, what plays nicely into the hands of a television station that needs to entertain an audience on a weekly basis. I think though, I prefer his later books, the ones that actually take place prior to these events. I'll rely on the show to take me through its interpretation of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15567.The_Wishsong_of_Shannara__The_Original_Shannara_Trilogy___3_" title="The Wishsong of Shannara (The Original Shannara Trilogy, #3) by Terry Brooks" rel="nofollow noopener">The Wishsong of Shannara</a> in season two, but I think I will finally get back to reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2675261.The_Gypsy_Morph__Genesis_of_Shannara___3_" title="The Gypsy Morph (Genesis of Shannara, #3) by Terry Brooks" rel="nofollow noopener">The Gypsy Morph</a>, the final book in his Genesis of Shannara series to see how this once earth comes to be.<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.bibliosanctum.com">www.bibliosanctum.com</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="13552610762457189759" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_713540040" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/713540040" />
    <a title="Evgeny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny"><img alt="Evgeny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544797852p2/9340136.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/713540040?book_show_action=true">Sep 06, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Evgeny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Evgeny" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny">Evgeny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9340136-evgeny?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer713540040" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14008851686117158832">An ancient tree created by elves who lost magic of that caliber a long time ago for the purpose of containing a great evil is dying. The said evil is about to escape with some of the most powerful guys already walking among population of Four Lands. Only Allanon knows the full extent of the problem, but even the last surviving druid cannot be at two places at the same time, so he must ask unlikely heroes for help - including Wil Ohmsford, the grandson of Shea Ohmsford from the first book. <br/><br/>This b</span>
  <span id="freeText14008851686117158832" style="display:none">An ancient tree created by elves who lost magic of that caliber a long time ago for the purpose of containing a great evil is dying. The said evil is about to escape with some of the most powerful guys already walking among population of Four Lands. Only Allanon knows the full extent of the problem, but even the last surviving druid cannot be at two places at the same time, so he must ask unlikely heroes for help - including Wil Ohmsford, the grandson of Shea Ohmsford from the first book. <br /><br />This book feels like Terry Brooks finally found his own voice as it is much further from Tolkien's writings in structure, plot, and characters. Something else I noticed: he is not shy of killing off characters - not to the extent of what <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/346732.George_R_R__Martin" title="George R.R. Martin" rel="nofollow noopener">George R.R. Martin</a> does, but in his case the killings start literally in the first pages of the book. It is also darker than both the first one and the whole Lord of the Rings trilogy. <br /><br />The characters in this book is interesting, or in case of the ones from the previous one (Allanon) are more interesting and flashed out. We have the druid's POV which really helps to understand his motives and makes him more human than countless wise wizards from other fantasy novels who never bother showing their motives to mere mortals - including the readers. <br /><br />Somebody already mentioned that the original trilogy must be judged after at least the second book, and I completely agree with this. The book is not perfect by any means, but it does deserve the status of being classic fantasy: 4 very solid stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14008851686117158832" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6502001963715554567">It took me almost a month to read this one! Not because it was awful, or difficult writing to wade through, but because I've been working 50-70 hrs a week. And I also wanted to take my time and enjoy the story. Believe it or not, of the three Terrys (Pratchett, Brooks, & Goodkind) I hadn't read anything by Brooks before. I attempted "Sword of Shannara" first but it was such a blatant ripoff of Tolkien that I didn't bother past the first chapter. As a cohesive story that is mostly original and st</span>
  <span id="freeText6502001963715554567" style="display:none">It took me almost a month to read this one! Not because it was awful, or difficult writing to wade through, but because I've been working 50-70 hrs a week. And I also wanted to take my time and enjoy the story. Believe it or not, of the three Terrys (Pratchett, Brooks, &amp; Goodkind) I hadn't read anything by Brooks before. I attempted "Sword of Shannara" first but it was such a blatant ripoff of Tolkien that I didn't bother past the first chapter. As a cohesive story that is mostly original and stands on its own, Elfstones fares very well. It's really different from the MTV show based on it, but I like them both in different ways. I loved Amberle most of all, even with all her fears and limitations -- she still managed to do the right thing. I feel like the Dagda Mor got defeated far too easily, but the truly creepy Mallenroh &amp; Morag made up for it somewhat. Overall, I'm going to say it was interesting. I didn't expect the twist with the Ellcrys and I'm going to read Wishsong to find out what happens next.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_1060821799" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1060821799" />
    <a title="Matt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31667052-matt"><img alt="Matt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589658539p2/31667052.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1060821799?book_show_action=true">Sep 21, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Matt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Matt" href="/user/show/31667052-matt">Matt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781101886052" href="/book/show/25489135-the-elfstones-of-shannara">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31667052-matt?shelf=shannara">shannara</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31667052-matt?shelf=2019-a-z-author-reading-list">2019-a-z-author-reading-list</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1060821799" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15949848058462643286">2020 re-read review. The Elfstones of Shannara is the 10th book chronologically in the Shannara series. There isn’t much I can add to my previous review, so I’ll just say I really love this book. Highly recommended!<br/><br/><br/>———————————————————————————<br/><br/>2019 re-read of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/39910203.The_Elfstones_of_Shannara__The_Original_Shannara_Trilogy___2_' title='The Elfstones of Shannara (The Original Shannara Trilogy, #2) by Terry Brooks' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Elfstones of Shannara</a>. <br/><br/>This is probably at least my 6th reading of Elfstones, and I loved every minute of it. What a great way to kick off my 2019 reading journey!<br/><br/>I have been a fan of the Shannara series and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/9629.Terry_Brooks' title='Terry Brooks' rel='nofollow noopener'>Terry Brooks</a> for 30 years now,</span>
  <span id="freeText15949848058462643286" style="display:none">2020 re-read review. The Elfstones of Shannara is the 10th book chronologically in the Shannara series. There isn’t much I can add to my previous review, so I’ll just say I really love this book. Highly recommended!<br /><br /><br />———————————————————————————<br /><br />2019 re-read of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/39910203.The_Elfstones_of_Shannara__The_Original_Shannara_Trilogy___2_" title="The Elfstones of Shannara (The Original Shannara Trilogy, #2) by Terry Brooks" rel="nofollow noopener">The Elfstones of Shannara</a>. <br /><br />This is probably at least my 6th reading of Elfstones, and I loved every minute of it. What a great way to kick off my 2019 reading journey!<br /><br />I have been a fan of the Shannara series and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/9629.Terry_Brooks" title="Terry Brooks" rel="nofollow noopener">Terry Brooks</a> for 30 years now, and his books will always be special to me. This is one of the books that really started my life-long love of reading, and I have to say that I love this story just as much now as when I first read it probably 30 years ago.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/39910203.The_Elfstones_of_Shannara__The_Original_Shannara_Trilogy___2_" title="The Elfstones of Shannara (The Original Shannara Trilogy, #2) by Terry Brooks" rel="nofollow noopener">The Elfstones of Shannara</a> and especially this version of the novel is a labor of love in two parts. I've read interviews of Mr. Brooks and he explains in his book <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15569.Sometimes_the_Magic_Works_Lessons_from_a_Writing_Life" title="Sometimes the Magic Works Lessons from a Writing Life by Terry Brooks" rel="nofollow noopener">Sometimes the Magic Works: Lessons from a Writing Life</a> how much time, effort, and re-work he had to do to get this story right. After his publication (and success) of his first book, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15575.The_Sword_of_Shannara__The_Original_Shannara_Trilogy___1_" title="The Sword of Shannara (The Original Shannara Trilogy, #1) by Terry Brooks" rel="nofollow noopener">The Sword of Shannara</a> in 1977, readers wanted a follow up/sequel to Sword. Mr. Brooks wrote one which was originally titled the <b>Song of Lorelei</b>, but his editor basically made him re-write the whole thing over, because the plot just didn't work. Brooks recalls in <b>How the Magic Works</b> that he had to re-write and edit this numerous times. I can only imagine how frustrating that must have been to him. The end result of that additional re-work effort is this wondrous novel. I for one, am thankful for it. This book is magical. <br /><br />This version is a special limited edition, leather-bound copy printed by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4161354.Shawn_Speakman" title="Shawn Speakman" rel="nofollow noopener">Shawn Speakman</a> by Grim Oak Press. Being such a loyal, practically life-long fan of the Shannara series, I had to have this version. Shawn is a super fan of Terry Brooks and the Shannara series, and he also operates Terry's website: <a href="http://www.terrybrooks.net" rel="nofollow noopener">Terry Brooks' website</a>. This version has new illustrations by Marc Simonetti, and a beautiful fold out map of the Four Lands. It is one of my prized possessions in my personal library and I'm thankful for Shawn and Grim Oak for publishing this version. <br /><br />I won't go into a synopsis of the plot, because people who have read the book will already know it, and potential readers can get it from the book cover. I'll just say that it is epic fantasy at its finest. It is an extremely satisfying fantasy story with believable, relatable, characters, an unforgettable setting, and a plot that is very well devised and executed. 5 stars all the way!</span>
  <a data-text-id="15949848058462643286" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/127000-michelle-morrell?shelf=i-own">i-own</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1662069129" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9347953418733042488">I first read this in middle school (cough cough) years ago, but apparently forgot every single plot point. It wasn't until I watched the tv adaptation (fantasy 90210, not bad, quite glossy) that my interest was sparked again. <br/><br/>From reading Brooks's "The Word and the Void" series, I did know these take place in a post-apocalyptic Earth. But with all the massive backstory I missed between then and now, I was worried I'd be lost. I was pleasantly surprised at how I was able to enjoy it as a stand-al</span>
  <span id="freeText9347953418733042488" style="display:none">I first read this in middle school (cough cough) years ago, but apparently forgot every single plot point. It wasn't until I watched the tv adaptation (fantasy 90210, not bad, quite glossy) that my interest was sparked again. <br /><br />From reading Brooks's "The Word and the Void" series, I did know these take place in a post-apocalyptic Earth. But with all the massive backstory I missed between then and now, I was worried I'd be lost. I was pleasantly surprised at how I was able to enjoy it as a stand-alone, though, even with all the references to what must have taken place in the immediately prior book, "The Sword of Shannera." <br /><br />It was just what I needed to rekindle my love of epic fantasy. Elves and demons, magic and nature, sacrifice and courage, all hallmarks of the genre. So hallmark, in fact, that it could have easily slipped over into cliche. What I forgot is that Brooks is, under it all, a darn good writer, who knows how to weave humanity into his characters and physicality into every setting. I will absolutely read further.<br /><br />Thanks for the free book table at Emerald City Comicon for giving me this tome, and extra special goodness for the decrepit Space Needle on the cover.</span>

<div id="review_1699336867" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1699336867" />
    <a title="Scott" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/732181-scott"><img alt="Scott" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588955941p2/732181.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1699336867?book_show_action=true">Jul 15, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Scott" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Scott" href="/user/show/732181-scott">Scott</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781101886052" href="/book/show/25489135-the-elfstones-of-shannara">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/732181-scott?shelf=abandoned">abandoned</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1699336867" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7563538405155773270">The worst thing about this book is not that it's a Tolkien rip-off; it's that it's a tedious, badly-written Tolkien rip-off. It reads as if a young writer read a few fantasy novels, maybe played a little D&D, and then proceeded to write what he thought a fantasy novel should sound like. In other words, the style is very affected and pretentious. He also repeats himself a lot. At least Stephen King will wait a few pages before reminding you of something you already read; Terry will keep going ove</span>
  <span id="freeText7563538405155773270" style="display:none">The worst thing about this book is not that it's a Tolkien rip-off; it's that it's a tedious, badly-written Tolkien rip-off. It reads as if a young writer read a few fantasy novels, maybe played a little D&amp;D, and then proceeded to write what he thought a fantasy novel should sound like. In other words, the style is very affected and pretentious. He also repeats himself a lot. At least Stephen King will wait a few pages before reminding you of something you already read; Terry will keep going over it until he is sure that you got it the first time. Maybe the publisher asked for a longer book and Terry didn't understand that he was supposed to add more story, so he just went through and reiterated everything. <br /><br />Not only does the plot feel strangely familiar, but Terry's version is terribly contrived. There's no sense of danger after a while because whenever the protagonists get into a fix they are saved by one <i>deus ex machina</i> after another. If it's not the book's third-rate Gandalf, it's a never-before-mentioned earth spirit that relocates them to safety, or it's the Elfstones whose power is to do whatever is needed to save the protagonists in any situation. <br /><br />The characters are completely uninteresting. When one slightly interesting character shows up who might make things a bit sexier, she is left behind. (Those fools!) I think she might turn up again later, probably at just the right moment to miraculously save our protagonists, but I didn't get that far.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7563538405155773270" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_797325413" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/797325413" />
    <a title="David Sarkies" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5856247-david-sarkies"><img alt="David Sarkies" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470027282p2/5856247.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/797325413?book_show_action=true">Dec 22, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David Sarkies" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David Sarkies" href="/user/show/5856247-david-sarkies">David Sarkies</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780708880951" href="/book/show/1698637.The_Elfstones_of_Shannara">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5856247-david-sarkies?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer797325413" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16210823156421427844"><b>This book suffers from sequelitis</b><br/>30 December 2013<br/><br/>	I have noticed that a lot of people have rated this book higher than the first simply on the basis that unlike the first book it is not a carbon copy of Lord of the Rings. This I will admit is true, it is not a carbon copy, but as far as I am concerned, it is still Lord of the Rings, and moreso, it suffers from what I call sequelitis. First, consider that the book has as its main character a young man (Wil, who is related to Flick, the hero of th</span>
  <span id="freeText16210823156421427844" style="display:none"><b>This book suffers from sequelitis</b><br />30 December 2013<br /><br />	I have noticed that a lot of people have rated this book higher than the first simply on the basis that unlike the first book it is not a carbon copy of Lord of the Rings. This I will admit is true, it is not a carbon copy, but as far as I am concerned, it is still Lord of the Rings, and moreso, it suffers from what I call sequelitis. First, consider that the book has as its main character a young man (Wil, who is related to Flick, the hero of the first book), who has barely reached the age of majority, going off on a great adventure to save the world. This time the story is about an elven woman who is carrying the seed of a tree that has died and this seed needs to be replanted so that the tree can be reborn and the great evil banished from the world. Secondly, much of the book involves a huge battle between the armies of this great evil while Wil and his burden (the elf girl) go off and do their own thing, much in the same way that Frodo and Sam go off and do their own thing while the others fight against the forces of Mordor.<br />	The reason that I say that this book suffers from sequelitis is because, like most sequels, it is set after the original book (and in this case, it is fifty years) and it turns out the great evil that was defeated in the original book wasn't actually all that great because there is an even greater evil out there that must be defeated so that everybody may once again live in peace. Also, despite the fact that this is listed as the second book in a trilogy, it appears that a trilogy was never actually planned but came about due to the success of the first book, so a sequel is written so as to capitalise upon that success (something that we see all too often come out of Hollywood).<br />	What is interesting is that I have been forced to think about the idea of 'what is fantasy' recently because somebody actually asked me that question. I had to think about it, and have come to realise that modern fantasy is much different to what the original fantasy stories were. These days they are just a form of escapism and entertainment and do not come very close to what we would consider to be literature.<br />	When considering the origins of fantasy I generally look back centuries before Lord of the Rings was written: basically to the Ancient Greeks. Here we have what could be considered two foundations, first of all that of the myth, and secondly that of the allegory. The best example of the myth would be the Odyssey and with this story the original hearers would actually look up at Odysseus as a character after which they could model their lives. He was a hero in the true sense of the word because he was in fact a role model. These days with modern fantasy, such as this book, we would not be reading it to consider the protagonist as a shining example of humanity for which we can follow. This is certainly the case here, and in Lord of the Rings.<br />	The second form is what I would call allegory, and Plato's description of Atlantis is an example of this. Here Plato is creating an imaginary nation as an example of what he believes a good and just nation looks like. Allegory also takes a different form in that it is also satire. Lucian of Samotosa and Aristosphanes are examples of ancient writers using fantasy in that way, but then there are also modern writers, such as Jonathon Swift and C.S. Lewis. However I hesitate to consider Tolkien to be a form of allegory since he hated the idea.<br />	Tolkien, however, is not necessarily the father of modern fantasy either, because prior to him (and Lewis) we have stories such as Barsoom and Conan which, while not morality tales or allegory, they were fantasy, but more in the sense that they were adventure stories that would appear in boys magazines. The development of fantasy here was in essence the adventure, but in a sense it was taking the unknown to a new level. As the world became smaller, and the unknown (such as darkest Africa) became known writers would expand their horizons: Conan going to the mists of history, before the waters covered Atlantis, and John Carter leaving the confines of this world to explore the countless other worlds beyond our atmosphere.<br />	That, in the end, is what modern fantasy probably is, namely adventure stories set in the unknown, targeted at a specific set of interests. Gone are the morality tales and the allegories – they are not needed anymore in our postmodern world where everything is right, as long as it does not infringe upon the rights and health of other people – morality is no longer objective but subjective, and we see that shift as we move from the 80s fantasy of Eddings and Brooks, to the fantasy of the naughties with the likes of George R.R. Martin.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16210823156421427844" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1707441940" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1707441940" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1707441940?book_show_action=true">Jul 24, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Max" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Max" href="/user/show/48451466-max">Max</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1707441940" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5651165546034667808">This was a very enjoyable reread for me. This is a great fantasy story. The first time I read it, I hadn't seen the Shannara Chronicles series yet. I found that really enjoyable and it was also fun comparing the book to the series. Ofcourse the series is way newer, and so it's a lot more "popular" - there's more romance, more focus on the bad guy. But the series bring a new perspective to this story. Anyway, not here to review the series ofcourse. <br/><br/>Compared to the first book in the series, the Sw</span>
  <span id="freeText5651165546034667808" style="display:none">This was a very enjoyable reread for me. This is a great fantasy story. The first time I read it, I hadn't seen the Shannara Chronicles series yet. I found that really enjoyable and it was also fun comparing the book to the series. Ofcourse the series is way newer, and so it's a lot more "popular" - there's more romance, more focus on the bad guy. But the series bring a new perspective to this story. Anyway, not here to review the series ofcourse. <br /><br />Compared to the first book in the series, the Sword of Shannara, this one is better. It has an original storyline, characters that are more believable and it flows more. In the first book the writing style was almost always too describing. This book does that better, more show instead of tell. Also, the paragraphs and quoting makes this easier to read. I also loved that there were some illustrations in my version, not a lot but about five. They are well done and add to the overall mood.<br /><br />If I had to name something that I didn't like, it would be the witch sisters. I will not spoil their story but they are just Disney-style bickering bad queens to me, LOL! My favourite characters were Perk the Wing Rider and Stee Jans, the commander of the Free Corps. I also loved Ander Elessedil as he changes and "grows up" interestingly during the book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5651165546034667808" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText2387279906890186350" style="display:none">Barb and I read the first book of this trilogy, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15575.The_Sword_of_Shannara__The_Original_Shannara_Trilogy___1_" title="The Sword of Shannara (The Original Shannara Trilogy, #1) by Terry Brooks" rel="nofollow noopener">The Sword of Shannara</a>, together, back in the late 80s, and liked it well enough (though I considered it very derivative of Tolkien's LOTR saga). <span id="freeTextContainer17766809066269913206">If you picked up this book as a fan of MTV's The Shannara Chronicles, you may be in for a bumpy ride. I was the same; a big fan of the fantasy-dystopia series I bought this book wanting to experience this world and these characters all over again. The Elfstones of Shannara is VERY different from the tv show. Many of the plot points in the tv show simply don't exist here - and a lot of characters are missing too. However, this is not to say that the book is disappointing, in fact it's a hugely en</span>
  <span id="freeText17766809066269913206" style="display:none">If you picked up this book as a fan of MTV's The Shannara Chronicles, you may be in for a bumpy ride. I was the same; a big fan of the fantasy-dystopia series I bought this book wanting to experience this world and these characters all over again. The Elfstones of Shannara is VERY different from the tv show. Many of the plot points in the tv show simply don't exist here - and a lot of characters are missing too. However, this is not to say that the book is disappointing, in fact it's a hugely enjoyable fantasy novel. The core three characters are still here - Wil, Amberle, and Eretria, still very much like their tv counterparts. The basic structure of the story - the quest to save the Ellcrys tree and stop the demon horde is the back bone of the story. In the book we get more locations, more characters, more action, and more epic battles. <br /><br /><br />I loved the tv show and I loved this book, but they are very, very different. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17766809066269913206" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2938881939" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2938881939" />
    <a title="Baal Of" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1720603-baal-of"><img alt="Baal Of" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1231801765p2/1720603.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2938881939?book_show_action=true">Aug 19, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Baal Of" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Baal Of" href="/user/show/1720603-baal-of">Baal Of</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/8971268-the-elfstones-of-shannara">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720603-baal-of?shelf=fruit">fruit</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2938881939" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11010127689831704794">I read the first book of this trilogy a very long time ago. I don't remember why I didn't read any more of the books in this series, whether it was just lack of money, or getting distracted by other books and authors, or because I thought the first book was mostly a Tolkien ripoff. In any case, I picked this one up so that I can check the trilogy off on a list, and because my friends that I am staying with during vacation have a copy on their bookshelf in the guest room.<br/><br/>This is a pretty straight</span>
  <span id="freeText11010127689831704794" style="display:none">I read the first book of this trilogy a very long time ago. I don't remember why I didn't read any more of the books in this series, whether it was just lack of money, or getting distracted by other books and authors, or because I thought the first book was mostly a Tolkien ripoff. In any case, I picked this one up so that I can check the trilogy off on a list, and because my friends that I am staying with during vacation have a copy on their bookshelf in the guest room.<br /><br />This is a pretty straightforward fantasy with all the elements that have become stereotypical, including a variety of humanoid races, a clearly outlined quest for the main characters to pursue, items of power that come with a cost, a mysterious and powerful entity with potentially mixed motives acting as a guide and general badass, an ancient evil being unleashed, deception and conflict between various factions who really need to work together, large scale battles and sieges, and plenty of narrow and miraculous escapes. With all that in mind, it was a fun read. It isn't by any means great, but for vacation reading it worked well, and it was a pleasant contrast to the R. Scott Bakker book book I'm currently reading which is fantasy way over on the grimdark side of the spectrum. Brooks does manager to kill off a fair number of named characters, while maintaining an inner group of main characters who are clearly going to survive to the end. Most of the twists in the story, if they really could be called that, were pretty easy to see coming, and I wasn't surprised by anything in particular. The reveal of the spy within the elven court was painfully obvious right from the very beginning. Wil makes a lot of stupid decisions throughout his journey, but is constantly bolstered by either good decision and support from the his companions, or by the conveniently timed magical intervention of entities the King Of The Silver River. The worst character was Wisp with his pathetic and repetitive "I serve the lady" and his incessant crying. I was happy when he <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[got torn apart by the Reaper. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Initially I thought that the demons, who outnumbered the Elven, Dwarven, Human, and Troll defenders should have had an easier time of wiping everyone out, but my friend David pointed out that the demons were completely undisciplined, and that the humanoid defense was modeled after the Roman Legion. Good point.<br /><br />Addendum:<br />I almost forgot one little detail that was mildly annoying. Brooks' constant use of the the description "child's face" for Amberle, and then at least once for Wisp, if I remember correctly. It would have been nice if he could have injected some variety in the descriptions, but then maybe he was just following Tolstoy's lead with the fucking downy lip in <b>War And Peace</b>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11010127689831704794" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('KdrIbDvDnisRMSFF1mP3cUAuadaOsE2uI/aFuRKJEYLf6MWVj5dTMumquwJUBWtQZNdvJIaCF+kgkE9SGqJuHw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('1kKBJUEgvx5dQ8mMQwxUCCWzb+GVBhPiI3H0rpr1P+8gcIzc9XRyB6XYU8vBasgpAUppE500SaUgFz5Fkt5Acg==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer15883507737246059913">Terry Brooks was born in Illinois in 1944, where he spent a great deal of his childhood and early adulthood dreaming up stories in and around Sinnissippi Park, the very same park that would eventually become the setting for his bestselling Word & Void trilogy. He went to college and received his undergraduate degree from Hamilton College, where he majored in English Literature, and he received his</span>
  <span id="freeText15883507737246059913" style="display:none">Terry Brooks was born in Illinois in 1944, where he spent a great deal of his childhood and early adulthood dreaming up stories in and around Sinnissippi Park, the very same park that would eventually become the setting for his bestselling Word &amp; Void trilogy. He went to college and received his undergraduate degree from Hamilton College, where he majored in English Literature, and he received his graduate degree from the School of Law at Washington &amp; Lee University.<br />A writer since high school, he wrote many stories within the genres of science fiction, western, fiction, and non-fiction, until one semester early in his college years he was given The Lord of the Rings to read. That moment changed Terry's life forever, because in Tolkien's great work he found all the elements needed to fully explore his writing combined in one genre.<br />He then wrote The Sword of Shannara, the seven year grand result retaining sanity while studying at Washington &amp; Lee University and practicing law. It became the first work of fiction ever to appear on the New York Times trade paperback bestseller list, where it remained for over five months.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15883507737246059913" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
